    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1762179087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762179087" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1762179087?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1762179087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8800625497150548919"><i>"Comparison is the thief joy."</i> - Theodore Roosevelt<br/><br/>The above sentiment couldn't be more true, even in the context of comparing books. This comparison may be a small insult to these novels but for me, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18775247.Mr__Mercedes__Bill_Hodges_Trilogy___1_' title='Mr. Mercedes (Bill Hodges Trilogy, #1) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Mercedes</a> read like a less clever cross between <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6345999-death-note?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Death Note</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba' title='Tsugumi Ohba' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tsugumi Ohba</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614-you' rel='nofollow noopener'>You</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/202260.Caroline_Kepnes' title='Caroline Kepnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Caroline Kepnes</a>.<br/><br/>The dynamic between depressed, retired cop, Bill Hodges & your friendly neighborhood psychopath, Brady Hartsfield, is reminiscent of that between <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6345999-death-note?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>L & Light Yagami</a>. Two intelligent men caught up in </span>
  <span id="freeText8800625497150548919" style="display:none"><i>"Comparison is the thief joy."</i> - Theodore Roosevelt<br /><br />The above sentiment couldn't be more true, even in the context of comparing books. This comparison may be a small insult to these novels but for me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18775247.Mr__Mercedes__Bill_Hodges_Trilogy___1_" title="Mr. Mercedes (Bill Hodges Trilogy, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Mercedes</a> read like a less clever cross between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6345999-death-note?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba" title="Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Tsugumi Ohba</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614-you" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/202260.Caroline_Kepnes" title="Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Caroline Kepnes</a>.<br /><br />The dynamic between depressed, retired cop, Bill Hodges &amp; your friendly neighborhood psychopath, Brady Hartsfield, is reminiscent of that between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6345999-death-note?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">L &amp; Light Yagami</a>. Two intelligent men caught up in a game of cat and mouse, quickly moving pieces back &amp; forth on a chess board of "Who Will Catch Who?" <b>Except their story is not nearly as compelling.</b><br /><br />Brady is written similarly to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821614-you" rel="nofollow noopener">Joe Goldberg</a>. They're both hilarious in their excessive judgement of everyone around them. They're both overwhelmingly fixated on one individual. They both have weird ideas about what it means to be aroused. <b>Except Brady is not nearly as relatable.</b> <br /><br />It's <i>possible</i> that without having read these books prior to, I would've enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18775247.Mr__Mercedes__Bill_Hodges_Trilogy___1_" title="Mr. Mercedes (Bill Hodges Trilogy, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Mercedes</a> a bit more. But even without those comparisons, <b>this story fell flat for me.</b><br /><br />There was never a time while reading that I found myself wondering what would happen. <b>Which is kind of a bummer for a novel pegged as a Mystery/Thriller.</b><br /><br />It's as though the two main perspectives were not written <b>distinctly enough</b> to be convincing. Multiple times throughout, one character would decide to do something &amp; the other character would immediately think of <b>that specific thing</b> in the next chapter or two. Why? Because they're just that on the ball?<br /><br /><i>I'm not buying it.</i> The back &amp; forth between hero &amp; villain is supposed to be powerful and exciting. <b>It's not supposed to read like a script.</b> Instead of building suspense, it comes off as <u>cheesy &amp; predictable.</u> <br /><br />Not to mention for a murderous mastermind, <b>Brady is kind of an idiot?</b> From the synopsis, we know he stole a Mercedes, drove it into a crowd of folks, and evaded capture by the local authorities. However, none of his subsequent actions actually lead me to believe he's the same guy who committed that crime &amp; got away with it.<br /><br />He exhibits some capability with computers, but in general he seems too <b>impulsive &amp; hot-headed</b> to be much of a threat. Brady's characterization by association sort of weakens the effect of Hodges' ability as a detective. <br /><br />On top of that, Hodges does a <b>very poor job</b> convincing me that he truly has the best interest of the public at heart. Much of the time I was hoping he would break down and take the case to active police, but even at the risk of harming others Hodges is determined to occupy the vigilante role.<br /><br />My <u>absolute least favorite</u> aspect of this novel is the female characters.<br /><br />Unfortunately, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18775247.Mr__Mercedes__Bill_Hodges_Trilogy___1_" title="Mr. Mercedes (Bill Hodges Trilogy, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Mercedes</a> suffers from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Refrigerators" rel="nofollow noopener">Women in Refrigerators</a> syndrome. Most of the female characters in this novel are used <b>entirely for the benefit or characterization of the male leads.</b><br /><br />Take this quote:<br /><br /><i>"The woman he slept with after he'd come to a point in his life where he thought he'd never sleep with any woman again. The woman who made him laugh and gave him comfort. [...] The woman who wrinkled her nose at him and mocked his 'yeah.'"</i><br /><br />Notice how this paragraph is constructed entirely to explain the role of the female's importance to the male character, and not to explain her individual attributes. She's not the woman with an impeccable sense of humor, <b>she's the woman who made him laugh &amp; gave him comfort.</b> <br /><br />Without having read the book, this point may not be as apparent. The problem is, <b>I can't tell you a damn thing about this woman outside the context of her male counterpart.</b> <br /><br />If this wasn't enough, we're then treated to this lovely sentiment:<br /><br /><i>"Hodges has never even considered the idea that Mr. Mercedes might actually be Mrs. Mercedes. He supposes it's technically possible, and it would make a neat solution for an Agatha Christie novel but this is real life."</i><br /><br /><b>Oh wait, I forgot women don't actually kill people in real life?</b> Sure, you can cite statistics about male vs. female crime rates, but does it make sense for a retired cop with years of experience to relegate this possibility strictly to fictional circumstances? <br /><br />This novel was written in 2014, for God's sake. I realize that Hodges is a 60+ year old man, but seeing as he's the sympathetic hero of the tale I just can't get on board. <b>Neither the novel, nor the characterization would've suffered by omitting this line.</b> <br /><br /><i>So why 2 stars instead of 1?</i><br /><br />It's because this wasn't bad enough to fall that far from grace. It made me chuckle a couple of times &amp; it wasn't written terribly. <b>But I could've gotten the same thrill from turning on the television &amp; flipping to the nearest episode of <i>Law &amp; Order</i> or <i>CSI.</i></b><br /><br />As pointed out by my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a>, <i>"With a show like that, you're giving up an hour of your life. Not 14."</i><br /><br />Unfortunately, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18775247.Mr__Mercedes__Bill_Hodges_Trilogy___1_" title="Mr. Mercedes (Bill Hodges Trilogy, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Mercedes</a> <i>is just not</i> the intricately woven tale of murder &amp; mystery &amp; originality that I wanted it to be. It's entertaining to an extent, but it doesn't leave a lasting impression. It doesn't cause me to contemplate or question. <b>When the book runs out of pages, it doesn't continue to live in my mind.</b><br /><br />With this being my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a> book, I didn't go into it with any real expectations. I know he's hit &amp; miss even with some of his biggest fans, and so I intend to give his other books a chance! Perhaps a horror story next. <br /><br />Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a> for buddy reading this with me even though I was an asshole &amp; read it way too fast.<br /><br /><i><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/mary/977-mrmercedes" rel="nofollow noopener">This review</a> and other reviews of mine can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Nest</a>!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8800625497150548919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959272946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2594538503122003313">I can't deny that I still need to read a lot to get to know Stephen King's work in novels. Basically my contact with his work has been on the adaptations of his works on films, mini-series, and on, that in that regard it has been quite a lot since I have watched almost all the major adaptations made.<br/><br/>However, I thought that this book can be a priceless option since not only didn't require having read any other book before, but also, himself had described as his first "hard-boiled" detective novel</span>
  <span id="freeText2594538503122003313" style="display:none">I can't deny that I still need to read a lot to get to know Stephen King's work in novels. Basically my contact with his work has been on the adaptations of his works on films, mini-series, and on, that in that regard it has been quite a lot since I have watched almost all the major adaptations made.<br /><br />However, I thought that this book can be a priceless option since not only didn't require having read any other book before, but also, himself had described as his first "hard-boiled" detective novel, so, it meant that this supposed to be away from his traditional horror books (knowing well that he has written other kind of stories besides horror genre's pieces).<br /><br />Something that I truly like was that he did some references to other of his novels but using the film adaptations of them, in that way, it was clear to me that this story was in a different "universe" than the one of the previous horror novels that it's usual to have some "cross-over" references implying that the characters "exist" in the same shared book universe.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...a single moment of forgetfulness had led to horrific consequences.</i>
</b><br /><br />It was an odd experience, since while I need to read more material from Stephen King, I have read a lot by Dean Koontz, and I found several similarities on this story. I know that daring to comment something like that must be like compare a <i>Star Trek</i> novel with one of <i>Star Wars</i>, however I did found some elements traditional to get in Koontz's books: A smart dog, a peculiar female character on a prominent support role, a car chase (kinda), a psychotic killer, and there is must be something else, but so far, those are which came to mind now. Also, while this is supposed to be "first" by King on this genre, well, honestly, Koontz has written several novels on this narrative style, with a protagonist dealing with some wacko psycho killer who wants the protagonist to die, just that those were refering as horror novels, without a so clear "distinction" to be considered "hard-boiled" detective novel.<br /><br />That that gets me to another point. Honestly, I didn't felt it as a "hard-boiled" detective novel, or even a detective novel in a general sense. True, the protagonist is a detective, a retired police detective to be specific, but having a detective as protagonist doesn't make a book a detective novel in my opinion. Due that since the beginning you know who the antagonist is, you know who did the crime, and at least for me, the main fun in a detective novel is the struggling to find the culprit. But here, is basically a manhunt. True, he needed to use some deduction skills to find the identity of the killer (that it's kinda boring since one (the reader) knows it from the beginning) even to contact people to help him in doing that, that even that at some moments was maddening since some explanations of why the killer did his tricks were too obvious so waiting a lot of pages to certify something that you already know how was done was shocking (in the bad sense.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...almost never won a kewpie doll at the county fair.</i>
</b><br /><br />Another thing that I found odd is that well, I notice too much similarities on the antagonist with Norman Bates from <i>Psycho</i>, at least the film's Norman Bates (since I still need to read the novel to compare) but definitely the antagonist is nothing so fresh and/or original and well, it's Stephen King that we are talking about and I'd expect a more original character.<br /><br />I had struggles with the protagonist, not at first, he was doing quite well, but without spoiling, there is a crutial moment, when he is affected by an attack made by the antagonist where the result should be too shocking, but I didn't felt it in that way, he was able to think, he was able to start to give orders to his "sidekicks" in a very reasonable way, and honestly, I thought that he'd need at least a day, if not more to cope with what happened and then, to start to think in a counter-strategy. The story keeps telling to the reader that he is supposed to be sad, but honestly I felt it as cold as the antagonist.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>...most people are sheep and sheep don't eat meat.</i>
</b><br /><br />On the climax (don't worry I won't do spoilers) the protagonist isn't the "hero", I mean the one to catch with his own hands the evil antagonist and it's something done by the "sidekicks", and I think that there is a reason of why a character is the protagonist and why others are supportive characters and/or "sidekicks". <br /><br />And I think that the book had too much pages in a story like this one, investing pages in detailing sub-events that they aren't so relevant or that they could be narrated faster without so many details. Fewer pages and a faster tempo could increase the possitive impact of the overall story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2594538503122003313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_925752207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/925752207" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/925752207?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer925752207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8787040968565062501">A madman driving a Mercedes plows into a crowd of job seekers, killing eight and injuring many more. A year later, the retired detective formerly in charge of the case gets a letter from the killer, taunting him. Can retired Detective Hodges bring in the killer before he kills again?<br/> <br/>Stephen King tries his hand at writing a straight up thriller in this outing. Was he good at it? Of course he was. <br/> <br/>Mr. Mercedes is a page turner, a cat and mouse thriller pitting a retired detective against the one</span>
  <span id="freeText8787040968565062501" style="display:none">A madman driving a Mercedes plows into a crowd of job seekers, killing eight and injuring many more. A year later, the retired detective formerly in charge of the case gets a letter from the killer, taunting him. Can retired Detective Hodges bring in the killer before he kills again?<br /> <br />Stephen King tries his hand at writing a straight up thriller in this outing. Was he good at it? Of course he was. <br /> <br />Mr. Mercedes is a page turner, a cat and mouse thriller pitting a retired detective against the one that got away. Since King is pretty good at ladling out the suspense, Mr. Mercedes is a stripped down version of the usual King song and dance, distilled down to its purest form.<br /> <br />As with a lot of King books, the characters go to hell and back over the course of the book. Hodges is an overweight former detective contemplating suicide when the book starts and soon returns to his detective roots. Brady Hartfield is a 30-ish guy who still lives at home with some serious mother issues when he targets Hodges. The supporting cast wasn't all that deep but Jerome and Holly really stepped up at the halfway mark.<br /> <br />Shifting viewpoints is never something I'm a tremendous fan of but King does it well here, as does his use of the present tense. Hartfield is an unsympathetic villain for the most part and I couldn't wait for him to get what was coming to him. That's what you get when you plot to poison someone's dog, asshole!<br /> <br />Extra bonus points for mentions of It, Christine, and Judas Coyne from Heart-Shaped Box. If It and Christine are movies, could Mr. Mercedes be set in the keystone world of the Dark Tower series? Something to ponder.<br /> <br />It wasn't all roses and revolvers, however. The hated thriller insta-love was in full effect. There were a couple logical leaps I didn't care for and Hartfield's final fate was a little bit of a letdown.<br /> <br />I found Mr. Mercedes to be more enjoyable than Doctor Sleep and Joyland but it was never a "drop everything and read" kind of book for me. 3.5 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8787040968565062501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_786685169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/786685169" />
    <a title="Trudi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi"><img alt="Trudi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446613110p2/1416912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786685169?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudi" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi">Trudi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=pulpy-goodness">pulpy-goodness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786685169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5582200456008813991"><br/>This is a case where the star system really fails me, or I feel like I must explain my rating. Four stars does not make <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> one of King's best. In fact, stacked up against some of his better known works, it pales and withers fraught as it is with giant plot holes, some incredulous leaps in logic and a hero who behaves more moronic than heroic (if you want a list of these weaknesses look no further than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956439073' rel='nofollow noopener'> Kemper's excellent review </a> where he takes King to task on all these matters and more</span>
  <span id="freeText5582200456008813991" style="display:none"><br />This is a case where the star system really fails me, or I feel like I must explain my rating. Four stars does not make <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> one of King's best. In fact, stacked up against some of his better known works, it pales and withers fraught as it is with giant plot holes, some incredulous leaps in logic and a hero who behaves more moronic than heroic (if you want a list of these weaknesses look no further than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956439073" rel="nofollow noopener"> Kemper's excellent review </a> where he takes King to task on all these matters and more).<br /><br />Kemper has a point. King shouldn't be given a pass based on Constant Reader goodwill alone. If you're going to tackle a genre where others have excelled before you, you just better bring your 'A' game and be firing on all cylinders. And here, King most definitely is not. There are problems. A lot of them. Not the least of which is King's fanboy enthusiasm for the crime thriller genre and falling victim to so many of its tropes and letting other opportunities pass him by unexplored.<br /><br />And yet.<br /><br />I was able to extract a fair amount of thrill from this thriller. I became tangled up in the cat and mouse game played out between the retired detective and the psychopathic killer. Brady Hartfield is a pretty compelling villain with a twisted and tragic backstory that makes him one of King's most memorable bad guys in a loooong time. Everything I wanted to feel for the stupid shit villains in Under the Dome, I felt here in spades with Brady. He is positively hateful. And genuinely terrifying without being supernaturally powerful.<br /><br />Big spoilers ahead under the tag.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What bumped this from an average three star read for me to the more memorable four are two horrific scenes that I thought were so well done. First, Brady and his mom killing the baby brother. So gruesome and heartbreaking and absolutely chilling the way mom smothers him with a pillow as he lies there broken and defenseless on the basement floor. Second, the mother's death scene by strychnine. I should have seen that coming a mile off. Poisoned hamburger meat left in the fridge. But I didn't. And when Brady comes home and realizes what must have happened I feel like I was punched in the gut. Her prolonged suffering, while deserved, was excruciatingly awful. I actually couldn't help but be reminded of Thinner and the way that ends with the infamous gypsy pie. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So the four stars reflect my state of mind while reading it -- engaged, turning the pages, and needing to know how it was all going to shake out. I was hoping for a very different ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I wanted Brady to succeed and for Hodges to be destroyed by his choices and negligence and to eat a bullet in remorse (which would have had a nice symmetry considering he's suicidal when the story opens) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> -- alas, that is not the ending I got, but man, I was squirming in my chair HOPING King would have the ball sack to take it darkside. The dread and anticipation had to be enough however. And it mostly was.<br /><br />This is a pulpy beach read and as an experiment on King's part I think it succeeds despite some serious problems. I hear now that this is a projected trilogy and I have conflicted feelings about that. I don't need King to write crime thrillers. That's not why I started reading him thirty years ago, and it definitely isn't why I've kept reading him. There are others out there in this genre who have been doing it longer and better. I'd rather see him continue his efforts in the King universe, where the sun might be shining, but there's something black and slippery in the shadows. Where small towns hold close their secrets and all is normal and safe, until it isn't.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5582200456008813991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-stephen-king">z-stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-horror-gothic">genre-horror-gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706769038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2518597248719484693">This was a great book to read in October. There are horror elements in the story, but this is more of a mystery book. I felt like it was very well crafted by Stephen King. He is a master a characterization in my opinion. Each character is a well rounded person with their own motivations. <br/><br/>In this novel he focuses on a retired cop who doesn't know what to do with himself in retirement and a murderer that brings him out of retirement and gives him something to do. The opening scene is grisly and th</span>
  <span id="freeText2518597248719484693" style="display:none">This was a great book to read in October. There are horror elements in the story, but this is more of a mystery book. I felt like it was very well crafted by Stephen King. He is a master a characterization in my opinion. Each character is a well rounded person with their own motivations. <br /><br />In this novel he focuses on a retired cop who doesn't know what to do with himself in retirement and a murderer that brings him out of retirement and gives him something to do. The opening scene is grisly and then it's a whole other genre. This is a mystery. Stephen is excellent with the nuance of this story.<br /><br />Bill's neighbor Jerome is part of the story and Bill meets a family that play into the story. This is not a who dunnit. We know pretty early on who did it, but we do get to see how Bill figures it all out. The final person in the trio is Holly, a older women who acts like a child still with some issues. She is the most interesting character in the story in my opinion. <br /><br />Most of the characters are broken in some way in this story and the story explores how people deal with life with that broken piece. Some characters can pull it together and some are crazy. Jerome is the only character who doesn't really seem broken. He's getting ready to go to Harvard - so he's smart.<br /><br />I found myself thoroughly enjoying this story. I feel it is one of King's better works in recent years, not that I have read them all yet. This story drew me in and I couldn't stop. I wanted to know what happened and how it was going to go down. I was compelled by the story. Stephen is so gifted at writing his story. I will be going on with the Bill Hodges story. I feel like this was an excellent story and mysteries aren't really my genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2518597248719484693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13066783889486881401">Verdict is: This is lukewarm-at-best Stephen King. <br/><br/>Still, not as notoriously awful as more recent literary attempts (yuck Dr. Sleep yuck!). There is notable strength in the back story of the sociopathic killer. Also, a healthy handful of Stephen King elements that makes one chuckle for their inclusion in such a, well, pedestrianish tale of savagery & woe. Regular tokens such as the car-as-weapon, retiree-as-hero and death-of-secondary-protagonist midway are all happily included in this tome.</span>
  <span id="freeText13066783889486881401" style="display:none">Verdict is: This is lukewarm-at-best Stephen King. <br /><br />Still, not as notoriously awful as more recent literary attempts (yuck Dr. Sleep yuck!). Then the ratings started coming in, and boy were they polarized. I still didn’t bother reading any blurbs or reviews, I just braced myself and pre</span>
  <span id="freeText8901285915457497572" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com</a><br><br>When I first saw the cover art for <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> I thought , “Awwwww, how sweet – Stephen King wrote a book about a guy who drives an ice cream truck” ; )<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/de9aXvA" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>I didn’t bother to read the synopsis. I rarely do – especially when it comes to anything by King. He writes it. I read it. End of story. Then the ratings started coming in, and boy were they polarized. I still didn’t bother reading any blurbs or reviews, I just braced myself and prepared for the worst.<br><br>I’m telling all you King superfans right now to repeat the following mantra: “Stephen King <b>did not</b> write this. Stephen King <b>did not</b> write this. Stephen King <b>did not</b> write this.” Did it work? Are you sufficiently brainwashed? It seems strange that I need to even add this disclaimer. With all of the different stuff King has written in his 40 year career his fans should know to expect the unexpected. If you’re expecting a horror story – you’re going to be seriously disappointed, so just pretend a Lee Child or a Harlan Coben or a Dennis Lehane wrote this book so you can give it the stars it deserves.<br><br>Bill Hodges is a Det-Ret (that’s retired police detective in layman's terms) who let one big fish get away. He’s now dipping his toes in the amateur private investigator arena – kind of a Philip Marlowe, if you will.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Bdo1bPI" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406210632ra/10519863.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <i>“In a don’t-give-a-fuck world, [Brady] is about to become the ultimate don’t-give-a-fucker.”</i>
</b><br><br>Can Hodges make the (not-exactly-legal) collar one last time and catch Hartfield before he strikes again?<br><br>After reading approximately eleventy billion mysteries over the years, I've become pretty good at figuring out the “whodunit” part, so I need a book that either takes me on a wild ride to the finish or one that assumes I’m not brain-dead and lets me know who the bad guy is right from the jump. Stephen King did both. Yes, right before the climax everything kind of turns into a giant stew of boiling shit and unbelievable plotline, but really <i>who even gives a flying fart?</i> because it’s Stephen Fucking King and even when he’s writing something he doesn’t generally write, he does it better than 99% of the other authors out there.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/MV2B31y" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2394592704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2394592704" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2394592704?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444788624" href="/book/show/20895196-mr-mercedes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2394592704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2796206750999221224">"Everybody likes the ice cream man."<br/><br/>Retired cop Bill Hodges is haunted by an unsolved crime where innocent people were waiting for entry into a job fair when a lone driver plows through the crowd in a Mercedes, injuring and killing many. When he receives a letter from the perp threatening another evil act, Hodges becomes hellbent on preventing such horror happening again.<br/><br/>I could read true crime until it made my eyeballs bleed, but there's just something about crime fiction or detective stories t</span>
  <span id="freeText2796206750999221224" style="display:none">"Everybody likes the ice cream man."<br /><br />Retired cop Bill Hodges is haunted by an unsolved crime where innocent people were waiting for entry into a job fair when a lone driver plows through the crowd in a Mercedes, injuring and killing many. When he receives a letter from the perp threatening another evil act, Hodges becomes hellbent on preventing such horror happening again.<br /><br />I could read true crime until it made my eyeballs bleed, but there's just something about crime fiction or detective stories that don't really appeal to me. So to know that King's Bill Hodges trilogy is kind of a cat-and-mouse detective story didn't fill me with much excitement. But let's cut to the chase - overall, I really enjoyed Mr Mercedes, but it is nowhere near being King's best.<br /><br />It's a page-turner and you constantly want to know what happens next, which propels you through the story. From the get-go we do know who the killer is, and that removes some of "mystery", but I liked getting into our villain's head - even though I fucking hate him with the passion of a thousand burning suns. I hated him until we got the backstory behind his younger brother, and then I REALLY fucking hated him, that part left me in tears.<br /><br />As for the other characters, Bill Hodges is one of my new faves. I don't know what it is about him exactly, but I just find him so lovable. I loved how he treats Jerome and Holly, and those around him. He's just very likeable and believable. I know Holly is a huge fan favourite for most people, and although I like her I do find her a bit irritating at times... I'M SORRY. Jerome is cool though.<br /><br />It's a strange read though. Some aspects feel very King, but others just don't feel like King at all. I'll start with those aspects that didn't feel very King-like: the lack of horror or a supernatural element (yes, it was quite unsettling at times and the methods used by our villain are terrifying but it's not PROPER horror), the storyline itself just felt un-King, the location...we're not in Maine or anywhere near it, it just didn't FEEL like a King location. However, King's fingerprints are all over it in terms of the development of his characters, the writing, and his dialogue. <br /><br />To me, Mr Mercedes felt like a well-written but kinda generic crime fiction book. It's a fun ride, but there's nothing overly substantial in there. However, this is part of a trilogy so I'm excited to see if this changes. That ending though *rolls eyes* It felt like I was watching a soap opera on a Friday afternoon and they had to make sure you tuned in on Monday. A tad cheesy and predictable. But it DID work in a way as I couldn't wait to pick up Finder's Keepers!<br /><br />You can see how my thoughts are all over the place with this one. In terms of sheer enjoyment, I would give it 4 stars out of 5, but I do have a few issues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2796206750999221224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730158435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9871676487077137008">Bill Hodges is a retired detective in a city that's seen better days. For that matter, Bill has seen better days himself. He's divorced, living alone, and now spends most of his time in his recliner watching dopey daytime television shows while playing with his gun and wondering what it might be like to just stick it in his mouth and end it all. He's let himself go to seed and is now twenty pounds overweight; clearly, he's on the downhill side of life.<br/><br/>Like a lot of retired detectives, though, Ho</span>
  <span id="freeText9871676487077137008" style="display:none">Bill Hodges is a retired detective in a city that's seen better days. For that matter, Bill has seen better days himself. He's divorced, living alone, and now spends most of his time in his recliner watching dopey daytime television shows while playing with his gun and wondering what it might be like to just stick it in his mouth and end it all. He's let himself go to seed and is now twenty pounds overweight; clearly, he's on the downhill side of life.<br /><br />Like a lot of retired detectives, though, Hodges is haunted by a handful of cases that he investigated but never solved. The one that pains him most involves a killer who stole a large Mercedes sedan and then deliberately drove it at high speed into a crowd of people who were lined up outside an auditorium, waiting for a job fair to begin. Eight people were brutally killed; many others were injured, and the driver got away cleanly.<br /><br />Now, several months later, Hodges receives a letter from the killer, taunting him and threatening to commit another act of atrocity. Of course, Hodges <i>should</i> turn the letter over to his former fellow detectives who are still investigating the massacre. But the letter stirs something in him and, rather than doing what logic and the law both require, he decides to investigate the matter himself.<br /><br />The reader soon learns the name of the killer, Brady Harstfield, and this story is as much his as it is Hodges. Hartsfield is a demented young man with some serious mommy issues. But he's very good with computers and has a certain native intelligence. He has a plan for Bill Hodges and a larger one for himself, stemming from the rush he got by killing all those innocent victims at the job fair.<br /><br />What follows is a great contest of wits and physical skills, pitting Hodges and a couple of unlikely allies against Hartsfield. In Hodges, Stephen King has created a flawed but convincing and engaging protagonist. In Harstfield he has created the epitome of an evil man. Books like this almost always rise or fall based on the qualities of the bad guy, and King provides us here with a believable and genuinely scary villain. Readers will not soon forget either Bill Hodges or Brady Hartsfield.<br /><br />If the book has a flaw, it rests with the fact that the reader has to buy into Bill's reasons for refusing to turn this matter over to the cops so that the entire police force can be deployed against Brady Hartsfield before a lot more innocent people are killed. There are several places in the book where the reader may wind up shaking his or her head at the notion that Hodges would continue to go it basically alone. But a lot of thrillers like this require a suspension of disbelief and the story moves along rapidly enough that it's easy enough to do so here. Bottom line, this is a great read from a man who obviously knows how to tell a story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9871676487077137008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2207025031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3218227605901567710">While no doubt global and domestic terrorists and active shooters have caused most of the damage, this book makes me wonder how much Stephen King has contributed to our national paranoia.<br/><br/>He comes up with some f***ing creepy s***.<br/><br/>I mean, we KNOW it’s Stephen King and he cannot just keep scaring us with the same old themes, he’s got to come up with new stuff. But even considering that, I was still shocked a couple of times and thought “who thinks like that”???<br/><br/>Stephen King, that’s who.<br/><br/>Mr. Mercedes </span>
  <span id="freeText3218227605901567710" style="display:none">While no doubt global and domestic terrorists and active shooters have caused most of the damage, this book makes me wonder how much Stephen King has contributed to our national paranoia.<br><br>He comes up with some f***ing creepy s***.<br><br>I mean, we KNOW it’s Stephen King and he cannot just keep scaring us with the same old themes, he’s got to come up with new stuff. But even considering that, I was still shocked a couple of times and thought “who thinks like that”???<br><br>Stephen King, that’s who.<br><br>Mr. Mercedes is not his traditional horror genre forte, this is rather a crime novel with horror elements intrinsic to the action. And one way of looking at crime fiction would lead to the thought that the best crime fiction should have horrific elements: murder, violence, insanity, etc.<br><br>Something else any self-respecting crime / thriller writer MUST have is a good protagonist. They cannot all have Sam Spade or Mike Hammer, but a good, likeable, charismatic hero. And this hero has to be real, we need to see some damage and world weariness. Doesn’t have to be a drunk, but maybe he used to be. Doesn’t have to be divorced, but he usually is; at least have a self-destructive path of broken relationships.<br><br>For his granite jawed, big hearted, street wise but broken leading man, King introduces us to Bill Hodges, a recently retired career detective. Bill is not adjusting well to his new idle time; there is a daily cavalcade of daytime TV and much staring into the abyss.<br><br>And all great super sleuths must have a nemesis, a criminal mastermind to act as a foil to our leading man. As Hodges is to Holmes, so too is the Mercedes Man to Moriarty. Taking his queue from recent headlines, this antagonist is a demented urban terrorist who wants to one up the 911 assholes as producing the greatest body count on American soil.<br><br>Having set the table, King serves up a banquet of hunt and hunted, with a big heaping plate of disturbing and a dessert of OMYGOD!<br><br>Good, solid crime fiction.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561840984i/27744144._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="359" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <span id="freeText3520152097879888243" style="display:none">Sorry for being sentimental, however; I am probably in the most depressive state I have ever been within. This book has helped me, bizarrely as it is about a "hard-boiled" ex-cop and a well-created mother loving charismatic and clever serial killer.<br /><br />I do not give many books five stars and Stephen King with his commercial success - I did not think this day would ever come except perhaps the Dark Tower series which I did appreciate. <br /><br />I can't start to analyse how good this is. Bill Hodges is a great character, he is there watching daytime TV until he gets a letter from the one case that got away whilst he is eating the business end of a revolver he loves and keeps on his couch.<br /><br />So many great scenes - I do not wish to disclose spoilers but the relationship with Brady and his mom, the relationship with Hodges and the sister of a lady who committed suicide following on from taunts from Brady (the Mercedes killer) under the fictional discreet chat room of the Blue Umbrella. <div id="review_3401760766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3401760766" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3401760766?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=library">library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3401760766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10132077048451591368">Another challenge I set myself at the start of the year was to return to some authors I hadn’t read in years. Stephen King certainly fits the bill as I haven’t read anything of his in over 15 years or more. Mr. Mercedes seemed like it would fit nicely as it’s mystery, not horror. <br/>Bill Hodges is a retired detective. One of the cases he never solved was who drove a Mercedes through a crowd of folks waiting for a job fair to open. When he gets a letter from the perk (sic) he decides to resolve the </span>
  <span id="freeText10132077048451591368" style="display:none">Another challenge I set myself at the start of the year was to return to some authors I hadn’t read in years. Stephen King certainly fits the bill as I haven’t read anything of his in over 15 years or more. Mr. Mercedes seemed like it would fit nicely as it’s mystery, not horror. <br />Bill Hodges is a retired detective. One of the cases he never solved was who drove a Mercedes through a crowd of folks waiting for a job fair to open. When he gets a letter from the perk (sic) he decides to resolve the case himself. He’s helped by Jerome, an exceptionally bright 17 year old young black man that does chores for him and Janey, the sister of the Mercedes owner. And finally, Holly, Janey’s somewhat warped cousin. Holly, who gets the best line in the whole book. “Holly, what are you doing?” “Therapy.”<br />We also hear from Brady Hartsfield, Mr. Mercedes Man himself. I will put Brady right up there with Joe Goldberg from You, as one of the creepiest bad guys out there. <br />This doesn’t rank up there with The Shining or The Stand, but it’s truly engaging, with great characters. In fact, the depth of the characters impressed me the most. Well, that and a great sense of tension throughout that ratchets up as the end approaches. King also employs just the slightest hint of snarky humor. It does require a certain suspension of belief that a Ret Det would go off the rails as a Lone Ranger and hide his discoveries from his former partner. <br /> I was shocked to find I had listened to this 14 ½ hour audiobook in just five days. That gives you an idea of how engaging this book truly is. Bring on book two! <br />Will Patton was a great narrator. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10132077048451591368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

MERCEDES by SPEPHEN KING was an action-packed, fast-paced, and highly enjoyable crime/mystery novel that held my interest from start to finish.<br/><br/>I started off listening to the audio version of this book but I wasn't able to get into the story like I needed to so decided that it would be best that I read the print copy instead.   <span id="freeText17070234119855943302" style="display:none">MR. MERCEDES by SPEPHEN KING was an action-packed, fast-paced, and highly enjoyable crime/mystery novel that held my interest from start to finish.<br /><br />I started off listening to the audio version of this book but I wasn't able to get into the story like I needed to so decided that it would be best that I read the print copy instead. The narration was really good by Will Patton but with books like these I tend to get distracted really easy and miss a lot of key points.<br /><br />I was expecting a little bit more excitement when it came to the climax though but I think that might have been my fault a little as I wasn't able to contain myself and I had to skim ahead a little to make sure it was going to end the way I wanted it to. Which I know did spoil the excitement a little for me. I was satisfied with the way the book ended though. <br /><br />I really enjoyed all the characters and look forward to re-visit them in the next book in this trilogy FINDERS KEEPERS.<br /><br />All of Brenda &amp; my reviews can be found on our sister blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a></span>

<div id="review_1775434646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775434646" />
    <a title="Annemarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie"><img alt="Annemarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593255949p2/27544490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1775434646?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annemarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annemarie" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie">Annemarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9783453438460" href="/book/show/51838849-mr-mercedes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775434646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6144669032237482054">There's something I need to mention beforehand:<br/>I was in a giant reading slump last year and read less books than ever before. I made it one of my biggest New Year's resolutions to get back on track. So I made sure to pick a book by my favourite author as my first read of the year. <br/>However, I was still nervous that I might not be able to get out of my slump, especially because I normally don't read detective stories anymore. I used to read them constantly when I was younger, but after a while I g</span>
  <span id="freeText6144669032237482054" style="display:none">There's something I need to mention beforehand:<br />I was in a giant reading slump last year and read less books than ever before. I made it one of my biggest New Year's resolutions to get back on track. So I made sure to pick a book by my favourite author as my first read of the year. <br />However, I was still nervous that I might not be able to get out of my slump, especially because I normally don't read detective stories anymore. I used to read them constantly when I was younger, but after a while I got tired of them. It seemed like they all followed the same pattern. They often had unbelievable plot twists, which came out of nowhere and were over the top. I found myself rolling my eyes and being annoyed. That's definitely NOT how I want to spend my reading time, so I stopped picking them up.<br /><br />But I mean, this is Stephen King, right? I was sure he could create a detective story I'd enjoy. And well - (unsurprisingly) I was right! FINALLY I read about a detective that didn't leave me in utter disbelief. Sure, Bill Hodges still shares some of the traits (and dare I say, "clichés") that are included in the majority of the books of this genre. But he had enough charm to make me like him. And he had enough other character traits to make him realistic. I enjoyed reading his internal monologues, how he came to his conclusions and so on. All the other characters made an impression on me as well - they all harmonized in the perfect way. <br />The suspense was on every page, no sentence was too much or unnecessary, I kept guessing what would happen next, I didn't want to stop reading - so all the things that are supposed to happen while reading a good crime book finally happened to me again! <br /><br />I went into the book almost completely blind, I only knew what would happen in the very first chapter. And I think this was the perfect way to experience the story. There were many things I didn't expect to happen, but they all made sense and didn't come out of thin air.<br />So yeah, I'm definitely glad I gave this genre another try! I couldn't have chosen a better book to start off the new year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6144669032237482054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_966923078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966923078" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/966923078?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=thriller-mystery-suspense">thriller-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966923078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer244376105914063969">For a suspense thriller this was pretty average, and for a Stephen King novel it's pretty weak. <i>Mr. Mercedes </i> is a departure from most of Mr. King's other work in the sense that it has none of his trademark mixture of the fantastic with the ordinary - it is a pure thriller, dedicated to James M. Cain and prefaced with the opening line of his noir classic, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25807.The_Postman_Always_Rings_Twice' title='The Postman Always Rings Twice by James M. Cain' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Postman Always Rings Twice</a>.<br/><br/><i>Mr. Mercedes</i> opens somewhere in the American Midwest, in a depressed, unnamed town hit hard by the recession. A</span>
  <span id="freeText244376105914063969" style="display:none">For a suspense thriller this was pretty average, and for a Stephen King novel it's pretty weak. <i>Mr. Mercedes </i> is a departure from most of Mr. King's other work in the sense that it has none of his trademark mixture of the fantastic with the ordinary - it is a pure thriller, dedicated to James M. Cain and prefaced with the opening line of his noir classic, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25807.The_Postman_Always_Rings_Twice" title="The Postman Always Rings Twice by James M. Cain" rel="nofollow noopener">The Postman Always Rings Twice</a>.<br /><br /><i>Mr. Mercedes</i> opens somewhere in the American Midwest, in a depressed, unnamed town hit hard by the recession. A crowd of desperate, unemployed people lines up in a long queue outside the door of a job fair hours before it opens, hoping to finally find a job. But they never will - before the fair has a chance to start a masked maniac in a Mercedes rams into the crowd, killing eight people and injuring fifteen. The killer escapes.<br /><br />A year later retired detective Bill Hodges lives out his retirement by eating crappy food and spending days in front of the TV. Hodges was one of the detectives assigned to capturing the job fair killer, and the failure to do so still sits heavily on his conscience. When Hodges receives a message from someone who identifies himself as the Mercedes Killer, Hodges decides to pursue him himself rather than turning the case over to the police, which soon turns into a desperate race to stop him before he strikes again on a much bigger scale.<br /><br />The biggest flaw of <i>Mr. Mercedes</i> is that there's literally nothing to distinguish it from countless run-of-the-mill thrillers which appear on the bestseller lists every week. There are tens of thousands of novels exactly like this one published every day across the world, and I'd dare to say that many of them are significantly better.<br /><br />The characters - which are often hailed as Mr. King's greatest achievements - have no real charm or personalities which would allow us to care about them and what they do. Bill Hodges is presented as a rogue detective who is hellbent on catching the killer on his own, even when he proves to be dangerous to innocent people. It simply makes no sense to not involve the police at this point, and Hodges's action are selfish and stupid - but he's constantly presented as a good character. There's an attempt at justifying this decision by making it personal, but it's so stupid and far-fetched that I can't believe no editor pointed it out.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Essentially, Bill Hodges - a 65 year old, overweight and somewhat grumpy loner instantly hits it off and develops a relationship with a much younger and attractive woman - sister of the woman whose car Mr Mercedes stole. She falls for Hodges almost instantly, and is then killed by Mr. Mercedes. The old trope of a detective hooking up with a hot woman in a thriller is so old and overused, and it's here only to justify Hodges's obsession with capturing the killer on his own as an act of vengeance. There's no chemistry between the two characters who both have nothing in common except knowing a dead person, and the love scenes are so absurd and silly that I couldn't believe that they were actually happening. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The rest of the characters are not great either - from Hodges's neighbor, Jerome, a black teenager who oddly begins speaking in Ebonics when having a dialogue with Hodges (but it's OK, since as Mr. King repeatedly points out he's very smart, and a future student of some ivy league school) through Holly - a slightly odd and neurotic female character, to the Mercedes Killer himself, who is the biggest disappointment of all in the book. How many times are we going to deranged male psychopaths, who are nothing more than a collection of disgusting and gruesome features that writers thrown into a sack on which they write their names? You know, the usual calm types who are secretly pedophiles and sadists, most of whom were abused as children and had incestuous experiences, etc. I felt as if I was reading a Dean Koontz novel, who made a career of writing such types and has written literally dozens of books featuring this exact model of villain. Also, why do mainstream thrillers almost never have female villains with these exact characteristics? Don't female perverts, sexual predators and sadists with daddy issues exist? It would be a much different and more interesting experience to create, write and read such a character. This is a field where women are seriously underrepresented. <br /><br />The story is slow and unsurprising - although I don't pretend to be an authority on suspense fiction there were no twists that I couldn't see coming from a mile away. It's also poorly plotted, as events happen and characters act in ways which are forced upon them, only to solve otherwise unsolvable situations (see spoiler). Holly, the neurotic and odd character, is also conveniently a computer genius who helps Hodges finds clues which were missed by his already smart sidekick, Jerome. How am I supposed to suspend my disbelief when I can see the author's hand on every page?<br /><br /><i>Mr. Mercedes</i> is what I would call an unnecessary book, as it adds absolutely nothing to its author's ample oeuvre, or the genre that it sits in. To make it worse, it ends on a note which promises a sequel, and two have already been announced - but I'm not enthusiastic about them at all. Stephen King has written some of my favorite books of all time, and the second star is only from my great sympathy for his person and his work. But unless Mr. King picks up his game and spices up these stories to make them stand out from the vast crowd, I really wouldn't bother.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="244376105914063969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17564145341036863339" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469048941i/19775299._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>

I mean he got off on what he had done. Literally. And once again we have another reference to "Pennywise" in the book as he was wearing a clown mask that looked like "Pennywise" !!!! ♥<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469048941i/19775301.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This "Mr. Mercedes" is beyond crazy! He is an evil genius and he works two jobs while being crazy and said genius. And God! What is with the creepy ice cream trucks! I will never get anything from an ice cream truck again! I read so many books with some crazy stuff with ice cream trucks. I do love it though. Just sayin' ☺<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469048941i/19775302.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bill Hodges is a retired cop and gets a letter from Mr. Mercedes. This begins the story of a cop trying to outwit a psycho. They communicate through a chat room and Hodges starts to slowly unravel who this maniac is with the help of some awesome people. <br><br>My favorite character in the book is Jerome. I loved Janey and Holly later on too. But Jerome cuts Hodges lawn and he's a super smart kid. I mean super smart. He will be able to get into any university he wants and he could already get any job in electronics he wants but he has his own ideals. <br><br>Mr. Mercedes steals Mrs. Trelawney's Mercedes and proceeds to run over a large group of people in line for jobs. Mrs. Trelawney feels guilty over this as she thinks it's her fault, that maybe she left her keys in the car and that's how he got the car. But there are so many different things that happened and the poor woman suffered for it. <br><br>Hodges meets Mrs. Trelawney's sister Janey and they get a little something going on. She has hired him to help find out more information in the case. <br><br>Hodges doesn't tell his old cop partner until the very end when all things go a little more around the bend. I keep wondering about that because he put some people in danger including young Jerome. Well, Jerome was 17/18 but still and some people did get killed. <br><br>Some of the story line about Mr. Mercedes was just horrible. He was horrible since a child, brought up horrible. Lets just say his mother probably didn't help on his becoming a wacko! <br><br>There was a point that I was getting really upset about what Mr. Mercedes was planning and then it was like karma took over. I had to say it was lovely in a morbid way. I had this feeling that was going to happen, it involved hamburger meat, but that is all I'm saying. <br><br>I liked the book and I look forward to seeing what is going to happen in the next two books. Or maybe I won't 0_0<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469048941ra/19775303.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/07/mr-mercedes-by-stephen-king.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17564145341036863339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6365754746217293545">This book was...hahaha, yeah right, this book hasn't even come out yet!<br/>I wish I read it...maybe I can time travel...<br/><br/><a href='http://s44.photobucket.com/user/theinnocentfireball/media/tumblr_lx0aglz5Cj1r8058ko1_500.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText6365754746217293545" style="display:none">This book was...hahaha, yeah right, this book hasn't even come out yet!<br>I wish I read it...maybe I can time travel...<br><br><a href="http://s44.photobucket.com/user/theinnocentfireball/media/tumblr_lx0aglz5Cj1r8058ko1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><br>Stephen King you sly dog you, you have done it once again! This book, no lie, starts off slowly, but you don't care, because his writing it so amazing that you are just entranced by that fact alone. <br>I once again did not read ANYTHING about this book so I went into it blindly and I am glad that I did. I enjoyed the hell out of this book. I found it nearly impossible to set down. It's not like his usual stuff which is just fine and dandy with me. No supernatural anything in this one. It was nice and refreshing to read a crime novel by King. <br><br>I also found out today that it's going to part one in a trilogy. Which any other time I would have been overly happy about it, but when I finished it I thought it was a stand alone and I loved how it ended just as is...<br>That's not saying that I won't read the next two once they come out. ;)<br></span>

<div id="review_2015600634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015600634" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015600634?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26309699-mr-mercedes">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Orient by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=bloody-romance">bloody-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=recs-by-anish">recs-by-anish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=hero">hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=desperado">desperado</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015600634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12070463489000187016"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496593182i/22931375._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Quote from “The Shining”<br/><br/>A thrilling rec from my GR friend, <b>Anish</b>. Thank you 😊 <br/><br/>This is my second King I’ve read. The first one was “The shining”, I was amazed, terrified and discouraged to read King’s books further. Apparently till now :) It seems I just needed a lighter take from King and I got it in “Mr. Mercedes”.<br/><br/>This cop-killer chase is overwhelming and merciless. The suspense is highlighted using the means of speech, words in bold, words in capital letters or italic to emphasize the urgency</span>
  <span id="freeText12070463489000187016" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496593182i/22931375._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Quote from “The Shining”<br><br>A thrilling rec from my GR friend, <b>Anish</b>. Thank you 😊 <br><br>This is my second King I’ve read. The first one was “The shining”, I was amazed, terrified and discouraged to read King’s books further. Apparently till now :) It seems I just needed a lighter take from King and I got it in “Mr. Mercedes”.<br><br>This cop-killer chase is overwhelming and merciless. The suspense is highlighted using the means of speech, words in bold, words in capital letters or italic to emphasize the urgency. And the world, the pop culture and it’s spoiled side, ups and downs, iPads, online dating sites, boy bands and a lot more. The beauty of this book lies there, in the need of happiness living a simple life, suffering the downfalls like unemployment and lack of money, and of course a masterful cat-mouse game between the killer and the ones who want to catch him. <br><br>The killer is a product of this world, socially inexperienced, crazy geek-freak with a creepy relationship with his mom( It could put Oedipus into amateur position for sure). Just add a <b>
  <i>“genetically handsome fellow with neatly combed brown hair and a bland say-cheese smile”</i>
</b> to this description And that makes him the most fascinating character. The dialogues which he has with himself are a pure example of a sneak peak into killer’s mind, whose self-pity leads into anger and hatred with the outcome – a ruthless childish killer (Who is to blame? Def not him! That’s a mind of a child). <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496593182i/22931376._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A sneak peak from the new TV-series coming this August! 😊 <br><br>For such a mastermind killer, there is a need of a fitting shrewd opponent. One is a retired detective. Divorced and spending his days aimlessly watching TV and playing hide-and-seek with his gun, he’s revived to life and saved from suicide by the very same killer who was a part of his trouble – one of unresolved cases. Such a charmingly true character. Moreover, his partner, a cool and smart kiddo with IT knowledge. I loved their dialogues and the accent of “Tyrone Feelgood Delight.” They represent the new and old world with such a delightful take. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496593182i/22931377._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A sneak peak from the new TV-series<br><br>This book has a view to the different kind of crazy, too. I mean people with emotional disorders, the struggle they have and it was good to see that this book showed the different angles to their fates.<br><br><br>“Mr. Mercedes” isn’t scary the way “The Shining” was for me, but it’s chilling and believable.This is a tense and synchronized story with lots of manipulation and sentimentality. The crimes presented there, are merciless and unforgiving and what scared me a lot is the credibility of them. While reading “Mr. Mercedes,” I felt like in a dejavu as I heard of such things on the news. Such as the recent accident in Manchester. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.snopes.com/2017/05/23/children-among-victims-ariana-grande/">http://www.snopes.com/2017/05/23/chil...</a> What drives seemingly sane people to do such barbaric things? And it goes on and on, that’s terrible. <br><br>Am I hooked on King? IDK, I’m not sure. I liked his characters and this book was interesting to read. The one and only thing I didn’t like was the suspect and all the evidence served to me on the golden plate. I like to kick my brain and try solve the mystery, search for hidden clues myself. But I must add credit to King, “M. Mercedes” has it’s charm, I kept guessing will everything go according to the plan and it’s nice, adds a thrilling feeling. Not enough to fall in love, but enough to continue with the series.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12070463489000187016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
